## 🟢 BC ORDERS READER — NEAR-REAL-TIME LATENCY (PM-RULED 2026-06-16, Kouros "à chaque commande immédiat")
**Operator directive: the BC open-orders sync must feel per-order/immediate, not 15-min — logistics works the Commandes board LIVE and can't keep up with a 15-min lag.** PM VERDICT: this is a LATENCY-TUNING decision with ZERO COGS/SOT risk (the reader is the INTENT-layer refresher; it NEVER writes status/status_events — depletion keys on operator-set `status='shipped'` only; `ord_orders` never feeds COGS/COP/WAC/BOM/beer-tax). NB this is a DIFFERENT lane from the Shopify-ingest "host fragility not frequency" ruling (§Shopify VPS rehome, line ~186): the BC-orders reader is ALREADY VPS-resident (`/etc/cron.d/maltytask-bc-orders`, MySQL local, no tunnel), so for THIS cron frequency genuinely IS the lever.
- **OPTIONS:** A=BC webhook subscriptions (event-driven; cost = public endpoint + 5s validationToken handshake + renewal cron for ≤3-day-TTL subs + missed-notification recovery + don't-trust-payload GET-the-resource security). B=tighten poll to `*/1`. C=hybrid (webhook + low-freq safety-net poll).
- **🔑 RECOMMENDATION: ship B (1-min poll) NOW; do NOT pre-build A.** A 60s worst-case lag is imperceptible to a human picker; A's marginal latency win (≤60s→~2s) is not felt, while its overhead (subscription-expiry = SILENT-death failure mode worse than a poll that just retries next minute; new public attack surface; renewal-cron fragility) is permanent. The robust end-state IS C, but C is only worth building if 1-min latency proves to ACTUALLY hinder the team. The poll is NOT throwaway: under C it becomes the mandatory 15-30min safety-net leg covering missed notifications / sub-expiry. So B is the foundation of every option.
- **🔴 MANDATORY with the frequency bump = `flock` single-flight guard.** At 15-min an overlap was impossible; at `*/1` a slow run (token refresh + larger open set) can exceed 60s → two importers race the same upsert (real divergence risk — this, not the frequency itself, is the unsafe part). House idiom (already used by `maltytask-kpi-recap` + `maltytask-ingest-recap`): `flock -n /tmp/maltytask-bc-orders.lock <cmd>` (`-n` = skip if a run is still going; next minute catches up). Importer itself is idempotent (echo-leg `mt:<id>`→`bc:<No>` + collision guard + full-open-set pull; no `--order` flag — full pull is cheap, ~29 rows).
- **CRON EDIT:** source = `db/cron/maltytask-bc-orders.cron` in the maltyweb repo (NEVER the deployed `/etc/cron.d/*` — overwritten on deploy). New line `*/1 … flock -n /tmp/maltytask-bc-orders.lock /usr/bin/python3 /var/www/maltytask/scripts/python/ingest_bc_sales_orders.py --apply >> /var/log/maltytask/bc-orders.log 2>&1` (drop `cd`, use absolute path, OR keep `cd && flock -c '…'` if the script is cwd-dependent — verify first). Update header rationale + flock note. Deploy via `bin/deploy.sh --apply` AFTER confirming the shared tree is clean (parallel sessions live; deploy pushes the WORKING TREE). Verify: `/etc/cron.d/maltytask-bc-orders` shows the new line; watch one clean 1-min cycle in the log; `ps -ef | grep ingest_bc` shows no overlapping runs.
- **IF C is ever built (reference, not now):** endpoint `public/api/bc-order-webhook.php` (greenfield JSON endpoint, NOT a `require_login` page; self-authenticates via `clientState` secret in `config/bc.env`, e.g. `BC_WEBHOOK_CLIENT_STATE`); echo `?validationToken` as text/plain <5s on subscribe; never trust payload → GET the resource via existing `bc.env` OData creds; renewal cron `db/cron/maltytask-bc-webhook-renew.cron` daily (2-day slack on ≤3-day TTL), flock-guarded, MUST alarm to the operator-visible failure channel on failure (silent-death mode); fast-return via dirty-marker + the safety-net poll (avoid php-fpm exec of Python — empty-PATH + ownership hazards). Demote the then-existing `*/1` poll to `*/15`-`*/30` safety-net.
- **EQUIP:** `coder`+`sql` for the cron edit (step 1 is a one-line cron change + flock wrap + deploy verify — `coder` alone covers it; cite the flock single-flight idiom + commit-before-deploy/clean-shared-tree discipline). Add `webapp-testing` ONLY if/when the webhook endpoint (C) is built.
- **SEQUENCING:** (1) ship B+flock now → (2) re-evaluate after the team works live days — only if 1-min lag is genuinely felt → (3) build C (webhook + demote poll to safety-net).
- **Trigger** "per-order"/"immédiat"/"near-real-time"/"webhook"/"15-min"/"1-min"/"poll frequency"/"latency"/"flock"/"subscription"/"bc-order-webhook" → this section.

## ✅ BC ORDERS READER — DELIVERY-DATE SEMANTICS FIX + LEAD-TIME TRACKING — SHIPPED 2026-06-15 (commit `9e2adfb`, LOCAL; mig 368)
**Corrects the fulfilment date that feeds the burn/couverture engine + the displayed "jour d'enlèvement". Reader-only edit — touches `ingest_bc_sales_orders.py` + mig 368 (NOT the 4 cage-session files).**

> 🔁 **REVISED 2026-06-17 — `requested_date` SOURCE NOW POSTING_DATE-PRIMARY (Kouros-APPROVED, deployed+verified, NOT committed).** The 06-15 fix below set `requested_date ← Document_Date` as a single source; that is now SUPERSEDED by a **cascade `Posting_Date → Document_Date → Shipment_Date`** (Posting primary; Document_Date kept as 1st fallback; never fall straight through to Shipment alone). `order_created_date ← Order_Date` unchanged. Rationale: Posting_Date is the operator's effective loading/delivery date and is the cleaner primary. **BC SONDE (read-only, 2026-06-17):** `Posting_Date` IS exposed on the OData `SalesOrder` web service (date fields available: Document_Date, Posting_Date, Order_Date, Shipment_Date, Due_Date, Promised_Delivery_Date, Requested_Delivery_Date, VAT_Reporting_Date, …); across 20 open orders **Posting_Date populated 20/20, 0 empty, 0 divergence Document_Date vs Posting_Date** in the current snapshot (consistent with "generally identical, but not always"). **CODE CHANGE:** internal var + dict keys renamed `document_date` → `posting_date` (9 sites: pull.append, detect_collisions map/gate/report, echo-leg UPDATE, upsert UPDATE/INSERT, backfill); the collision report label `bc_ship_date` is KEPT but its value now comes from `posting_date`. **NO migration** (pure read-point change; `requested_date`/`order_created_date` already exist). **DEPLOY:** surgical per-file (rsync→/tmp→`sudo install -o maltytask -g www-data -m 644`), md5 deployed==local, `py_compile` OK — NOT `bin/deploy.sh` whole-tree (shared-clone dirty under parallel cage/expeditions sessions). **BACKFILL:** `--backfill-dates` dry-run = **0 update needed** (Posting==Document everywhere today → stored requested_date already correct); no `--apply` ran. Forward-only: the `*/15` cron picks up Posting_Date the moment a divergence appears. 10 invoiced orders outside the open endpoint = untouchable but already shipped/closed. **NOT git-committed** — shared/dirty maltyweb clone; commit+push is Kouros's call (stage ONLY `scripts/python/ingest_bc_sales_orders.py`, pathspec never `-A`). 🔴 **RESIDUAL RISK (low):** the "0 divergence" snapshot is only 20 open orders today — the cascade is designed for exactly the day Posting≠Document, so the divergence path is unproven against live data; first real divergence should be spot-checked (Posting wins, Document is the fallback). Burn/couverture engine + "jour d'enlèvement" + lead_days all now key off Posting_Date via `requested_date` — semantics unchanged, just a better-sourced date.
- **🔴 ROOT CAUSE (Opus-audited LIVE):** the reader mapped `ord_orders.requested_date ← BC `Shipment_Date``, but BC leaves `Shipment_Date = Order_Date` (creation day) on **24/25** orders; header AND line `Requested/Promised_Delivery_Date` are EMPTY (**0/25**). The REAL delivery/loading-at-client date is BC **`Document_Date`** — operator convention: *"la date du document est la date de chargement/livraison chez client"*; populated **25/25**, differs from creation in **21/25**. The 2026-06-15 BC-sole-source cutover dropped the delivery date the retired WeeklyOrders sheet used to carry → **burn/couverture (semaines_stock, forward seasonal sim) + the "jour d'enlèvement" were running on CREATION dates** (systematically early — false-early demand timing).
- **FIX:** `ingest_bc_sales_orders.py` now maps `requested_date ← Document_Date` on the INSERT leg, the refresher UPDATE leg, AND the echo-leg; collision date-compare aligned to Document_Date. Backfilled existing bc rows via `--backfill-dates` (**10 updated, 1 skipped: ORD210069 gone from the endpoint**).
- **🆕 LEAD-TIME TRACKING (out-of-process orders — Kouros: late / same-day orders must be flagged; normal ask = 24-48h processing).** **mig 368** adds `ord_orders.order_created_date DATE ← BC `Order_Date`` (backfilled). The flag is **DERIVED, NO stored column:** `lead_days = DATEDIFF(requested_date, order_created_date)`; convention `<=0` jour-même (critical), `<2` tardive/sous-48h (warning), `>=2` normal. **🔴 Threshold MUST live in a `system_settings` row** (section `'fulfilment'`, e.g. key `order_lead_time_warning_days` default 2) — to be created in the UI phase, **NOT hardcoded** (house rule: never hardcode a system setting).
- **VERIFIED (Opus):** requested_date == Document_Date on live orders; `lead_days` across all 11 bc orders correct, **zero negative anomalies, all 3 tiers present (2 jour-même · 3 tardive · 5 normal).**
- **✅ UI BADGE SHIPPED 2026-06-15 (commit `3b69225`, on origin; mig 369 `369_fulfilment_lead_time_thresholds.sql`) — closes this fix.** `expeditions.php` Commandes board shows **⚡ <24h (critical, incl. jour-même / negative-lead anomaly) / ⏱ 24-48h (warn) / ≥48h none.** `lead_days = DATEDIFF(requested_date, order_created_date)`, **DERIVED at display (NO stored column).** Thresholds in `system_settings` section `'fulfilment'`: `order_lead_time_critical_days=1` + `order_lead_time_warn_days=2` (réglables — house rule honored, NOT hardcoded). NULL `order_created_date` → no badge. Smoke-verified: **2 critical / 3 warn / 5 normal.** 🔴 **IMPLEMENTATION NOTE (durable): `expeditions.php` needed an explicit `require_once` of `app/settings.php` at top — `system_setting()` was NOT transitively loaded.** (Don't assume the settings accessor is in scope; grep before calling it from a page that doesn't already pull it.)
- **NB:** the EMAIL-ORDER INGESTION arc is now UNDER WAY — Build B SCHEMA + SCAFFOLDING SHIPPED 2026-06-15 (migs 370; `646e18c`/`0c0bb5e`), see email-order-ingestion-arc.md §AS-BUILT. Still gated externally (Gmail DWD super-admin → Arthur; real per-sender parsers → Kouros sample .eml).
- **Trigger** "jour d'enlèvement"/"date de chargement"/"Posting_Date"/"Document_Date"/"Shipment_Date"/"lead time"/"jour-même"/"tardive"/"sous-48h"/"order_created_date"/"requested_date semantics"/"couverture date" → this section (read the 06-17 REVISED banner at top first — Posting_Date is now the primary source).

**FRAME:** Phase 1 (read pull BC open orders → ord_orders, cron `*/15`) is LIVE (now incl. id=142/143/144 first --apply; was 4 bc rows pre-go-live), `source='bc'`, connector `scripts/python/ingest_bc_sales_orders.py`, cron `/etc/cron.d/maltytask-bc-orders`. This program makes maltytask the OPERATIONAL source of truth on top of BC (accounting record). Governing principle = operational metric ≠ accounting ledger: stock/COGS derive from maltytask operational truth; BC = invoiced/shipped reality (locks at BL/posting) + reconciliation. **🔴 `ord_orders.requested_date` = BC `Posting_Date → Document_Date → Shipment_Date` cascade (Posting primary; delivery/loading-at-client), NOT raw `Shipment_Date` — fixed 2026-06-15 `9e2adfb` (Document_Date), REVISED 2026-06-17 to Posting-primary cascade (deployed, NOT committed); see the BC ORDERS READER section directly above.**

**LIVE-STATE VERIFIED 2026-06-15 (PM probe), load-bearing for this program:**
- `ord_orders` = pure BC-mirror today (no operational-vs-mirror field split, no `origin` col beyond `source`). Cols as enumerated in the Phase-1 §. `ord_order_lines` = `order_id_fk,sku_id_fk,qty,line_comment` — **NO line_status col, NO BC-line snapshot.**
- **🔴 NO BC line-snapshot store exists.** The connector pulls `SalesOrderSalesLines`, resolves `(bc_item,uom)→sku_id`, writes `ord_order_lines`, and DISCARDS the BC line representation. Build B's divergence detection (maltytask line ≠ BC line) has nothing to diff against → B REQUIRES persisting a BC line snapshot (per-line: bc_no, line_no, bc_item, uom, qty, resolved sku_id) so "what BC holds" is retained alongside "what maltytask holds".
- **🔴 CONNECTOR DEVIATES FROM PHASE-1 RULING 4:** as-built it AUTO-ADVANCES status to `bl_printed` on `Completely_Shipped=True` (`should_advance_to_bl_printed()`, cron comment confirms). Ruling 4 said `Completely_Shipped` is a reconciliation SIGNAL surfaced on the board, NEVER an auto status write. This is a STANDING divergence to resolve as part of B (it writes unauthorized status from a pull). NB it does NOT fire depletion (fg-stock Step 4 keys on `status='shipped'` only, which the pull never writes) — so no double-deplete today, but it IS the pull writing operator-owned status.
- **fg-stock Step 4** (`app/fg-stock.php`) sums ALL `ord_order_lines.qty` for `o.status='shipped'`, NO line-status filter. → Build C MUST add the line-status exclusion here or 'non_livre'/'rupture' lines deplete physical stock. (Also appears in snapshot Leg 1 ~L628/647/718/1079 — the predicate must stay symmetric; grep all `ord_order_lines` reads.)
- **Manual form** `public/modules/expeditions.php` POST handler (L348, `view=form`): writes `order_type ∈ customer|internal`. `order_type='customer'` = the B2B double-entry path. `internal` (taproom/cage/shop/eshop-manual) is legitimately maltytask-native. Edit mode `?view=form&edit=<id>` read-only when status∈shipped|cancelled.

**RULING — DATA MODEL (decision 2):** ord_orders evolves from "BC-mirror" to "operational record that may be BC-fed". Field classes:
  - **BC-mirror (pull-owned, refresher-gated on status∈entered|confirmed):** customer_id_fk, requested_date, transporter_id_fk, comment, line qtys+SKUs. NEVER status/status_events (operator-owned, ruling 4).
  - **maltytask-operational (NEVER flow to BC):** status + status_events, line_status (B/C), divergence flag (B). 
  - **origin:** keep `source` as the origin discriminator (`bc` vs `web`/`import`/`email`); when Phase 2 lands, a maltytask-born order = `source='web'`(or new `source='maltytask'`) that maltytask CREATED in BC → it carries a `bc_no` once BC assigns one, but its origin stays maltytask. Do NOT overload `source='bc'` for maltytask-born-then-echoed orders (that's the echo-loop trap, see D).
  - **Corrections (Pepitium, B):** edit-in-place + FLAG, do NOT create a new line revision. ord_order_lines stays the live operational truth; the BC-line snapshot retains the divergent BC value; the `divergence_status` flag on the order says "maltytask ≠ BC, comptable correction required". Line-revision history lives in `ord_order_status_events`-style append log only if Kouros later wants an audit trail — NOT needed for v1.

**SEQUENCING (decision 1):** **A → (B ∥ C) → D.**
  - **A FIRST (small, urgent, stops active bleeding).** Block manual B2B (`order_type='customer'`) creation in the saisie form. DECISION: block-B2B-but-ALLOW-internal — `internal` orders (taproom/cage/shop/eshop-manual) are legit maltytask-native and have no BC source. Hide/disable the customer-order branch of `view=form` POST + UI; keep `internal` create; keep EDIT of bc-sourced orders (logistics still needs to correct lines — that's exactly what feeds B). Server-side reject `order_type='customer'` on create (defence-in-depth, not just hide the radio). ~0.5 day. Mig: none.
  - **B ∥ C (operational-layer additions, parallelizable, both small):**
    - **C (line status 'non_livre'/'rupture'):** mig adds `ord_order_lines.line_status ENUM('to_fulfil','non_livre','rupture') DEFAULT 'to_fulfil'` (or 2-val if rupture≡non_livre — confirm w/ Kouros whether they need to distinguish "supplier rupture" from "operationally undeliverable"). Excluded from fg-stock Step 4 + ALL ord_order_lines depletion reads (add `AND l.line_status='to_fulfil'`); NEVER flows to BC (it's a maltytask-only fact — nothing shipped); reportable as a backorder/lost-sales view on the Commandes board. ~1 day.
    - **B (divergence flag + BC line snapshot):** mig adds (1) BC line-snapshot store — prefer a sibling table `ord_order_bc_lines` (bc_no/source_ref, line_no, bc_item, uom, bc_qty, resolved_sku_id, snapshot_at) over widening ord_order_lines (keeps the two facts cleanly separable; schema_meta row required); (2) `ord_orders.divergence_status ENUM('none','correction_compta_requise') DEFAULT 'none'` (+ optional divergence_detail). Connector change: on each pull, persist the BC snapshot AND diff resolved BC lines vs current ord_order_lines → if they differ AND the order is frozen (status≥picked, ruling 4) OR an operator edited a line away from BC → set divergence flag + surface (Commandes badge + doc_review_queue type `bc-order-correction-required` for admin). Also RESOLVE the ruling-4 deviation here (auto-advance bl_printed → reconciliation signal, not status write). Operational truth (maltytask DGDB) drives stock/COGS; admin issues the BC credit-note+re-invoice manually (interim). ~2 days incl. the connector refactor + Opus-verify the snapshot/diff doesn't perturb the live status-preserving upsert.
  - **D LAST but STARTS IN PARALLEL as a spike (the big arc).** Architecture decisions below; build after A/B/C land the model it writes against.

**RULING — PHASE 2 WRITE-BACK ARCHITECTURE (decision 3), the hard parts:**
  - **(a) ECHO-LOOP:** maltytask creates order in BC → `*/15` reader pulls it back → MUST NOT duplicate. Mechanism = maltytask writes a maltytask-owned external ref into a BC field the reader keys on; reader's source_ref upsert (`bc:<No>`) is already idempotent on BC OrderNo, but the maltytask-born order has a LOCAL id BEFORE BC assigns a No. **Resolve by: maltytask-born order gets a provisional local source_ref (`mt:<localid>`); on successful BC create, store the returned BC No and REKEY source_ref → `bc:<No>` in the SAME write transaction; the reader then matches it as existing on next pull (UPDATE not INSERT).** Do NOT rely on External_Document_No for echo identity (see b).
  - **(b) 🔴 External_Document_No DUAL-USE COLLISION — FLAG:** Kouros ALREADY uses BC `External_Document_No` to distinguish SPLIT orders (same customer, different location). Writing maltytask refs into it would COLLIDE with that operational use. → Phase 2 must NOT hijack External_Document_No for the maltytask echo ref. Use a DISTINCT BC field (a custom field e.g. `MaltytaskRef`, or `Your_Reference`, or the Shopify-style `ShpfyOrderNo` pattern of a dedicated custom column) — confirm with Kouros which BC field is free. This is a hard prerequisite for D's create path.
  - **(c) IDEMPOTENCY + PARTIAL FAILURE:** every write carries the maltytask local id as the dedup key (the provisional ref); a create that times out but actually landed in BC must not double-create on retry → before create, GET BC by the maltytask ref; create only if absent. Wrap create+rekey in a local transaction; if BC create succeeds but local rekey fails, a reconcile pass (the reader) recovers by matching the BC ref back to the local provisional row.
  - **(d) CREDIT-MEMO (Pepitium):** create avoir (`salesCreditMemos`) for the wrong locked invoice + corrected re-invoice. Start with CREATE only (per Kouros: CREATE orders + credit memos; POST stays human in BC). The B-flag (`correction_compta_requise`) is the queue that feeds D's credit-memo generation.
  - **(e) BC API CHOICE:** standard `salesOrders` / `salesCreditMemos` POST (the standard Business Central v2.0 API) for CREATE — cleaner than OData web services for writes, supports the standard entity shapes. Reuse the S2S OAuth2 client-creds from `config/bc.env`. (The read side uses OData `SalesOrder`/`SalesOrderSalesLines` web services for richer fields; writes can use the standard API independently.) BC write permission = Kouros's BC-side permission-set change (SUPER role, Entra has API.ReadWrite.All) — he does it himself; we build assuming it lands. **Start with CREATE, NEVER POST (no posting/invoicing from maltytask initially — keep that human in BC).**

**RULING — PHASE-1 READER CHANGES when Phase 2 coexists (decision 4):**
  - Status-preserving upsert UNCHANGED in spirit (status operator-owned), but the reader must learn to RECONCILE maltytask-born orders: a pull row whose maltytask-ref matches a local `mt:`/rekeyed `bc:` row = UPDATE (the echo), never a new INSERT. → reader keys on the maltytask ref FIRST, then `bc:<No>`.
  - **Collision logic is NOT YET External_Document_No-aware (deferred per Phase-1).** With B/C/D: it STILL doesn't need External_Document_No for echo (we use a distinct maltytask ref, decision 3b). BUT — because External_Document_No legitimately splits same-customer/different-location orders — the reader must NOT treat two BC orders sharing a customer as one; it already keys on BC OrderNo (unique), so split orders stay distinct. **No change forced by B/C/D, but the deferred External_Document_No-awareness should be revisited IF Kouros ever wants the board to GROUP split orders — flag, don't build.**
  - `bc_completely_shipped → bl_printed` auto-advance: REMOVE it (ruling 4) as part of B; replace with reconciliation signal. Once removed, the reader never writes status at all — clean separation Phase 2 depends on.

**DIVERGENCE FLAGS (this program):**
  - **🔴 Echo-loop double-create** (D) — guarded by maltytask-ref-first reconcile + GET-before-create idempotency.
  - **🔴 External_Document_No dual-use** (D) — do NOT use it for echo identity; it's Kouros's split-order key. Use a distinct BC field.
  - **🔴 Double-deplete via new line statuses** (C) — fg-stock Step 4 + all ord_order_lines depletion reads MUST exclude non_livre/rupture; Opus independently verifies the no-deplete invariant (COGS/inventory-bearing).
  - **🔴 Breaking the LIVE Phase-1 reader** — B refactors the connector (snapshot + diff + remove auto-advance); regression-gate the status-preserving upsert (no unauthorized status writes, no spurious INSERT) before `--apply`. The reader is operationally hot (`*/15`).
  - **Parallel store** — `ord_order_bc_lines` (BC snapshot) is NOT a second copy of ord_order_lines; it is the retained BC-side fact for diffing. Keep them distinct-by-purpose; never let anyone "reconcile" them as one (they DIVERGE by design — that's the whole point of B).
  - **COGS coupling** — operational truth (ord_orders/lines, post-correction) drives fg-stock depletion + COGS; BC reconciled via avoir. A correction (Pepitium DGDF→DGDB) changes which SKU depletes → COGS-bearing → Opus verifies the corrected line depletes the right SKU.

**EQUIP per build:** A → `coder`+`ui`(+`webapp-testing` smoke the customer-create block + internal-create still works). C → `sql`+`coder`+`ui`(+`webapp-testing`) [DONE `59bd1f7`]. B → `sql`+`coder`(+`ui` badge +`webapp-testing`); COGS/status-bearing → Opus independent verify [DONE `2f0087e`]. D → `coder`+`sql`(+`webapp-testing`); spike the BC standard-API CREATE against a test order first; the credit-memo path is the careful part. **MIGRATIONS:** A=none; C=line_status ENUM on ord_order_lines (INSTANT) [357]; B=`ord_order_bc_lines` table (schema_meta row) + `ord_orders.divergence_status` ENUM [354/355]; D=likely `bc_no` col on ord_orders + the maltytask-ref handling (confirm at build). Re-`migrate.php --status` at build-start (parallel sessions lead; head was 357 + 59bd1f7). Trigger "block manual B2B"/"double-entry"/"Pepitium"/"correction compta"/"avoir"/"credit memo"/"non livré"/"rupture"/"backorder"/"write-back"/"Phase 2 BC"/"External_Document_No"/"echo loop"/"divergence flag order" → READ this section.

---

## §D LAUNCH-READY SCOPE — Phase 2 write-back maltytask→BC (PM-scoped 2026-06-15, A/B/C all landed)

> Greenfield. No BC-write code exists in either repo. D is OUTWARD-FACING (the first thing maltytask ever writes back to the accounting system) → **the disarm discipline below is non-negotiable: NO agent POSTs to BC live without Kouros's explicit go.** Built assuming Kouros's BC write perm-set lands; confirm the exact perm name (§3) before any live test.

**SPLIT D INTO TWO SUB-PHASES — D1 (order-create) ships and proves first; D2 (credit-memo) is the careful Pepitium path, built after D1's echo-loop+idempotency are proven live.** Reason: D1 exercises the WHOLE write spine (OAuth2 S2S create, provisional-ref → rekey, GET-before-create idempotency, reader-reconcile) on the simpler entity; D2 reuses that proven spine for the harder `salesCreditMemos` + DGDF→DGDB correction. Don't build D2 until D1's echo loop is verified non-duplicating on a live `*/15` pull.

### 1. BUILD STEPS — dependency order

**D0 — SPIKE (read-only, no writes, do FIRST):**
- Stand up an OAuth2 S2S token call against the standard BC v2.0 API (`/v2.0/companies({id})/salesOrders`) reusing `config/bc.env` client-creds — confirm the standard API endpoint authenticates with the SAME app reg the OData read side uses (the read side uses OData web services; the standard API is a different base path — verify the token scope covers both, this is the #1 spike risk).
- **GET-probe the chosen echo field is free across the live order set** (§3b): the prior probe found `Your_Reference` 0/21 empty — RE-RUN it at build-start (orders move). Pick the BC field for `MaltytaskRef` and confirm with Kouros it doesn't collide with anything BUT `External_Document_No` (which is reserved for his split-order key — HARD do-not-touch).
- Output: a dry-run module that can READ a salesOrder by the echo field and print "would create" — zero writes. Gate D1 on this passing + Kouros confirming the perm name + echo field.

**D1 — ORDER-CREATE (build after D0 + A/B/C):**
- **Schema (mig, confirm number at build — head 357+):** `ord_orders.bc_no VARCHAR(40) NULL` (the BC-assigned OrderNo, populated on successful create — distinct from `source_ref`); reuse `source` as origin (a maltytask-born order = `source='maltytask'` NEW enum value, or `'web'` — confirm; do NOT overload `'bc'`). The provisional/rekey identity rides on the EXISTING `source_ref` col (`mt:<localid>` → `bc:<No>`). schema_meta: ord_orders already classified — update its row note, no new table for D1.
- **Writer/worker module path:** `scripts/python/push_bc_sales_orders.py` (mirror the read connector `ingest_bc_sales_orders.py` — same `_load_bc_env`/`_get_token`/company-id resolution; standard-API base path for writes). Drains maltytask-born orders flagged for push. **`--dry-run` DEFAULT, `--apply` explicit, flock'd, cron DISARMED at ship.** (Python to match the existing BC connector toolchain, NOT a PHP handler — the BC integration lives in `scripts/python/`.)
- **What triggers a push:** a maltytask-NATIVE customer order created in the app. NB after A, manual `order_type='customer'` is BLOCKED in the saisie form — so D1's create source is whatever NEW maltytask-native B2B entry path Kouros wants (confirm: is there a maltytask-born B2B order in v1, or is D1 purely the echo-safe plumbing for a future entry path? A blocked all manual customer entry, so D1 may have NO live producer yet — clarify scope with Kouros; if no producer, D1 = build the spine + test against a synthetic flagged row, ship disarmed).
- **REKEY mechanism (echo-loop guard, ruling 3a):** maltytask-born order gets provisional `source_ref='mt:<localid>'` at creation. On successful BC create: in ONE local txn, store returned `bc_no` + REKEY `source_ref → 'bc:<No>'` + write `MaltytaskRef=<localid>` into the chosen BC field. The `*/15` reader (ruling 4) keys on the maltytask-ref FIRST then `bc:<No>` → matches the echoed pull as EXISTING (UPDATE, never INSERT).
- **IDEMPOTENCY guard (ruling 3c):** before every create, GET BC by `MaltytaskRef=<localid>`; create ONLY if absent. Wrap create+rekey in a local txn; if BC create succeeds but local rekey fails, the reader's reconcile pass recovers (matches BC ref → local provisional row). Every write carries the local id as dedup key.
- **Reader change (ruling 4 — already partly done in B):** confirm the connector keys maltytask-ref-first; B already removed the `bc_completely_shipped→bl_printed` auto-advance (reader writes NO status). D1 only adds the maltytask-ref-first match precedence if B didn't.
- **Excluded lines:** non_livre/rupture lines (C's line_status) MUST be EXCLUDED from the BC write — nothing operationally-undeliverable gets written to the accounting order. Filter `line_status='to_fulfil'` in the push payload assembly (mirrors fg-stock's depletion gate).

**D2 — CREDIT-MEMO (build after D1 proven live):**
- **Producer:** B's `ord_orders.divergence_status='correction_compta_requise'` flag (set when maltytask line ≠ frozen BC line, e.g. Pepitium DGDF→DGDB) is the QUEUE that feeds D2. D2 drains flagged orders.
- **Path:** create `salesCreditMemos` (avoir) for the wrong locked invoice + the corrected re-invoice, against the standard BC v2.0 API. Same OAuth2/idempotency/echo spine as D1 (GET-before-create on a memo-level ref; rekey). **CREATE ONLY — NEVER POST the memo** (posting/invoicing stays human in BC).
- **COGS coupling (ruling, Opus verifies):** the correction changes which SKU depletes (DGDF→DGDB) → operational truth (ord_order_lines post-correction) already drives fg-stock depletion; the avoir only reconciles BC. Opus independently verifies the corrected line depletes the RIGHT SKU before D2 writes anything.
- **Careful-path note:** credit-memo entity shape + the avoir↔re-invoice pairing is the riskiest write. Spike it read-only (GET an existing credit memo, map its shape) before any create.

### 2. DISARM / DRY-RUN DESIGN — what MUST stay disarmed until Kouros's explicit go
- **Both `push_bc_sales_orders.py` and the D2 credit-memo writer ship `--dry-run` DEFAULT; live write requires explicit `--apply`.** NO cron entry at ship (the file may exist in `db/cron/` commented-out or simply absent — DISARMED = no `*/N` schedule writing to BC).
- **Triple gate before any live `--apply`:** (i) Kouros confirms the BC write perm-set is live (§3); (ii) Kouros confirms the chosen echo field (§3b) is free + not `External_Document_No`; (iii) Kouros gives explicit "go for live BC write". Until all three: dry-run only, against a synthetic/test order, output = "would create {payload}" with the full JSON body printed for Kouros to eyeball.
- **PM standing order: NO agent issues a live BC POST/PATCH/create.** A build agent may build + dry-run + (with Kouros's go) run ONE supervised `--apply` against a single test order that Kouros nominates. Bulk/cron enablement is Kouros's hand only.
- **First live test = ONE order Kouros picks**, verified round-trip: create in BC → confirm `bc_no` returned + `MaltytaskRef` written → wait one `*/15` pull → confirm reader UPDATEs (no duplicate INSERT) → confirm no spurious status write. Only after that round-trip passes does D1 graduate from disarmed.

### 3a. ECHO-FIELD + READER-LEG RULINGS (PM 2026-06-15, D0-probe-driven — supersede the earlier "echo=Your_Reference" line)

**✅ D1 DONE + LIVE-PROVEN + DISARMED + COMMITTED (`7db6861` on main, LOCAL-ONLY — awaiting Kouros "push"; recorded 2026-06-15).** Both Opus-flagged design issues below were RESOLVED and a live supervised round-trip passed clean (Kouros-authorized, executed by Opus). AS-BUILT:
- **Resolution: Path A taken** (write via OData `SalesOrder` entity, echo = `Your_Reference`; `External_Document_No` left untouched/reserved for Kouros's split-order key — ISSUE 1 fork closed in favour of A).
- **Writer `scripts/python/push_bc_sales_orders.py`** (deployed): creates BC SalesOrder via OData `NAV.SalesOrder` + `SalesOrderSalesLines`; echo tag `Your_Reference='mt:<id>'`; GET-before-create idempotency on `Your_Reference`; atomic local rekey `mt:<id>`→`bc:<No>` + `bc_no` on success; ONLY `line_status='to_fulfil'` lines pushed (non_livre/rupture excluded — C dependency); DISARMED = `--dry-run` default, live needs BOTH `--apply` AND `--i-have-kouros-go`, NO cron. Admin helpers `--delete-bc` (composite key + If-Match) + `--make-test-order`/`--cleanup-test-order`.
- **Reader `scripts/python/ingest_bc_sales_orders.py`** (deployed, LIVE on the `*/15` cron): echo-leg added as precedence 1 (ISSUE 2 fix) — matches a pulled BC order by parsed `Your_Reference`→local PK REGARDLESS of `source_ref` state, rekeys in one txn, writes NO status/status_events (Ruling 4). Closes the race/rekey-failure duplicate gap.
- **Shared helper `scripts/python/bc_echo.py`** = `bc_echo_format`/`bc_echo_parse`, imported by BOTH connectors (namespace can't drift — [[feedback_canonical_list_call_not_copy]]).
- **mig 361 APPLIED** = `ord_orders.bc_no VARCHAR(40)` + `source` ENUM +`'maltytask'`.
- **LIVE ROUND-TRIP (2026-06-15):** synthetic maltytask order id=157 → live OData create → BC No=ORD210076, `Your_Reference='mt:157'` set, only the to_fulfil line (ALT4) pushed / rupture excluded → rekeyed local to `bc:ORD210076` → reader dry-run printed `[echo-leg] Would rekey local_id=157` + `Would INSERT: 0` (zero duplicate, no status write) → deleted ORD210076 from BC (composite-key + If-Match) → cleaned local back to 138. Nothing left in BC or DB.
- **🔴 CRITICAL BC-PERMISSION LEARNING (cost many cycles — durable):** writing sales orders via the BC API requires **`D365 BUS FULL ACCESS`** on the S2S app's BC user. `D365 SALES DOC, EDIT` + `POST` + `D365 READ` are NOT sufficient — they don't cover the API entity buffer table **5495 (Sales Order Entity Buffer)**, giving a MISLEADING `HTTP 403 … TableData 5495 … Insert` that looks like a missing sales-doc grant. (This SUPERSEDES the §3 guidance that `D365 SALES DOC, EDIT` is the load-bearing grant for D — see §3 note.) To EDIT the app's permission grid you must first set État=Désactivé, re-enable after (grid is locked while Activé — why earlier add-attempts silently failed). Azure side was fine throughout (token carried `roles=['API.ReadWrite.All']`).
- **Two code gotchas found+fixed during the test:** (1) `NAV.SalesOrder` has NO text `Comment` property (it's a boolean flag) → HTTP 400 if sent; (2) `NAV.SalesOrder`/`SalesOrderSalesLines` use a COMPOSITE key (Document_Type+No / +Line_No) and DELETE needs `If-Match`.
- **🔴 OPEN SCOPING (divergence flag — still stands):** D1 has NO maltytask-native order PRODUCER in v1 (block A removed manual customer entry). The writer is proven plumbing with NOTHING to push in prod until either D2's producer materializes OR a re-opened maltytask-born B2B entry path exists. Flag, don't paper over.
- **➡️ NEXT = D2 (salesCreditMemos for Pepitium DGDF→DGDB), which REUSES this proven spine.**

---
_Pre-D1 ruling history (resolved above; kept for the reasoning trail):_
**Built disarmed: writer `push_bc_sales_orders.py` + mig 361 (`ord_orders.bc_no` + source enum +`'maltytask'`) exist, Python-only, apply path raises NotImplementedError, nothing committed. Opus verification caught 2 design issues → PM ruled.**

**ISSUE 1 — echo field (REJECT the coder's `externalDocumentNumber`='mt:<id>' choice).** D0 found `Your_Reference` does NOT exist on the standard v2.0 write API (only OData `Your_Reference`); the only filterable echo on v2.0 is `externalDocumentNumber` = `External_Document_No` — which is RESERVED as Kouros's split-order key (HARD do-not-touch). So the coder's choice collides with a reserved field → rejected. FORK (one Kouros decision, re-run D0 first):
- **Path A (PREFERRED) — write via the OData `SalesOrder` entity (the SAME entity the reader reads), set `Your_Reference` there.** Keeps echo=`Your_Reference`, leaves `External_Document_No` free. Challenge the D0 "v2.0 is the only write surface" premise — verify OData `SalesOrder` accepts POST/PATCH under the S2S token scope. Clean: write+read leg ride the same entity/field, no standard↔OData identity gymnastics.
- **Path B (fallback, only if OData write not viable) — `External_Document_No` with strict `mt:` namespace, REQUIRES Kouros's explicit sign-off** (co-opts his field). Collision risk is REAL not moot: only ever write `mt:<id>` there pre-publish on maltytask-born orders that have NO customer external ref by construction; a maltytask-born order needing a real external ref = a DIFFERENT path, must not use this leg. Reader discriminates on `mt:` prefix. Strictly worse than A.
- **Field identity CONFIRMED:** standard-v2.0 `externalDocumentNumber` ≡ OData `External_Document_No` ≡ same BC SQL column; OData `Your_Reference` ≡ BC `Your_Reference` column. Whichever the writer sets, the reader adds the same-named field to its OData `$select` (L262) and sees it. (Reader uses OData `SalesOrder`/`SalesOrderSalesLines` entities, NOT v2.0.)

**ISSUE 2 — reader echo-tag leg is MISSING (real duplicate defect; coder's "uniq_ord_source_ref blocks it" claim is WRONG — `mt:<id>` vs `bc:<No>` are different keys, no collision).** Reader (`ingest_bc_sales_orders.py`) matches ONLY `existing_bc.get(f"bc:{no}")` (~L669), never the echo field → if `*/15` reader runs between BC-create and local rekey (or rekey fails), it INSERTs a duplicate + orphans the `mt:<id>` row. DESIGN (the missing ruling-4 leg):
- **Precedence in `upsert_order()` + every sibling helper resolving `existing` from `existing_bc.get(source_ref)`, first-match-wins:** (1) ECHO-TAG LEG (NEW, FIRST): parse echo field; if `mt:<id>` → look up LOCAL row by PK `id=<id>` REGARDLESS of its current `source_ref`; if provisional `mt:<id>` → REKEY in one txn `SET bc_no=<No>, source_ref='bc:<No>'` (recovery path); if already `bc:<No>` → plain header-refresh; either way return `"update"` → duplicate INSERT impossible (matched on invariant local id). (2) EXISTING `bc:<No>` LEG (current). (3) COLLISION/BACKLOG/INSERT (current) — only for genuinely new BC-originated orders.
- **Writes ONLY:** `bc_no`, `source_ref` rekey, `updated_at`, existing header-refresh fields. **NO status, NO status_events** (Ruling 4 — reader writes no status; status operator-owned).
- **Idempotent** (keyed on invariant local id) + **status-safe** (respect the SAME refreshable-status gate as the existing UPDATE; if matched row's status is beyond refreshable = operator picked/printed → key-recovery ONLY (`bc_no` + rekey if still provisional), NO header refresh, NO status touch, NEVER re-advance — mirrors leg-2 "frozen, key-only").
- **CONNECTOR-ONLY edit** (`ingest_bc_sales_orders.py` reader + `push_bc_sales_orders.py` writer); touches NONE of the 4 cage-session files. webapp-testing stays optional.
- **SHARED HELPER = MANDATORY:** one pair `bc_echo_format(local_id)->'mt:<id>'` / `bc_echo_parse(echo)->Optional[int]`, imported by BOTH connectors so the namespace can't drift ([[feedback_canonical_list_call_not_copy]] applied to the echo namespace — never inline `'mt:'+str(id)` on both sides).
- `bc_completely_shipped→bl_printed` auto-advance confirmed GONE — does NOT change this design, it's a PREREQUISITE the echo leg depends on (reader writes no status).

**COMMIT SEQUENCE (PM-ratified):** do NOT commit the current disarmed state. (1) Resolve ISSUE 1 with Kouros FIRST (re-run D0 OData-write probe → pick A or B → Kouros sign-off if B) — the field choice is a Kouros decision (touches his split-order convention), NOT a coder call. (2) THEN dispatch ONE coordinated coder: reader echo-tag leg + shared helper + writer sets resolved echo field via resolved surface. (3) THEN Opus independently dry-run-verifies the duplicate-prevention invariant (simulate broken path: local still `mt:<id>`, reader pulls `bc:<No>`+echo → assert UPDATE/rekey, zero INSERT) — COGS/order-integrity-bearing, not on sub-agent's word. (4) THEN commit the disarmed whole (both connectors + mig, `--dry-run` default, no cron). Live write stays triple-gated on Kouros.

### 3. BC PERMISSION / SCOPE NAME — confirm with Kouros BEFORE any live test
- **API auth scope (Entra/app-reg level):** the S2S app needs `API.ReadWrite.All` (application permission) on the Dynamics 365 Business Central API — Kouros said Entra already has it. CONFIRM it's `API.ReadWrite.All`, not the read-only `API.Read.All`. This is the OAuth2 scope the token request asks for (`scope=https://api.businesscentral.dynamics.com/.default`).
- **🔴 BC permission-set (in-product, per the S2S app's BC user) — CORRECTED BY D1 LIVE TEST (see §3a as-built):** the load-bearing grant is **`D365 BUS FULL ACCESS`**, NOT `D365 SALES DOC, EDIT`. EDIT+POST+READ do NOT cover the API entity buffer table **5495 (Sales Order Entity Buffer)** → misleading `HTTP 403 … TableData 5495 … Insert`. To edit the app's permission grid, set État=Désactivé first then re-enable. (The original guidance below was wrong — kept struck for the trail.) ~~For D1 we need `D365 SALES DOC, EDIT`~~.
- **§3b echo field:** confirm which BC field carries `MaltytaskRef` — `Your_Reference` (probed 0/21 empty) is the leading candidate; NOT `External_Document_No` (split-order key, reserved).

### 4. EQUIP line
**EQUIP D (D0 spike + D1): `coder` + `sql` + `webapp-testing`** (no UI surface in D itself — it's a backend connector; webapp-testing only if a push-status badge gets added to the Commandes board, otherwise drop it). D writes Python in `scripts/python/` (BC-connector toolchain) → `coder` covers it; `sql` for the `bc_no`/source enum migration + the reader-reconcile query. **D2 adds nothing to EQUIP** (same skills). **GATING: external-write + COGS/order-integrity-bearing → Opus INDEPENDENTLY verifies (a) the echo-loop produces NO duplicate on a live pull, (b) D2's corrected line depletes the right SKU, (c) every write is GET-before-create idempotent — sub-agent "it works" is a CLAIM.** Disarm discipline (§2) is a HARD gate, not advisory.

### 5. C DEPENDENCIES + SPLIT RECOMMENDATION
- **What D depends on from C:** D1's push-payload assembly EXCLUDES `line_status IN ('non_livre','rupture')` lines (only `to_fulfil` lines get written to BC) — this is C's column. C is DONE+LIVE (mig 357), so the dependency is satisfied. No other C surface is load-bearing for D.

- **SPLIT: YES — D1 (order-create) first, D2 (credit-memo) second.** D1 proves the write spine (OAuth2 create, provisional→rekey, GET-before-create, reader-reconcile, line_status exclusion) on the simple entity + the live echo-loop round-trip; D2 reuses the proven spine for the harder avoir/re-invoice + DGDF→DGDB correction. ## §RETURNED FG TRACKING (BC-DERIVED) — ARC AS-BUILT 2026-06-16 (P0+P1+P2+P3-SYNTHÈSE SHIPPED+LIVE; P3-RATE+P2b OPEN; 4 LOCAL COMMITS NOT PUSHED + 2 FRONTEND FILES DEFERRED-FROM-COMMIT)

**Scope (Kouros-APPROVED — BC-DERIVED PIVOT, supersedes the earlier order-XOR scoped design that was "to be written once Kouros approves").** Returns are **BC-derived**: the bookkeeper books an *avoir de vente* (credit memo) in Business Central → it imports to `inv_sales_ledger` as `doc_type='credit'` (also `return_receipt` for some). **BC OWNS REVENUE — the avoir reverses it; the app writes NO revenue/COGS-ledger entry.** The app owns DISPOSITION + physical FG only. **Default disposition = `quarantine`** (no FG effect until operator confirms restock).

**DISPOSITION TAXONOMY (per line, the cardinal decision) = enum extended to `restock / scrap / quarantine / rebate`:**
- `restock` = re-enters FG (resaleable) — the ONE FG/COGS-bearing leg.
- `scrap` = write-off (hygiene/best-before) — NO FG effect.
- `quarantine` = held pending decision (DEFAULT) — NOT yet in stock.
- `rebate` = a beer-credit that is a price/defect rebate, NOT a physical return — NO FG effect (added in mig 376).

**PM's earlier rulings CONFIRMED CORRECT against live data (recorded so nobody re-litigates):**
- `fg_stock_compute()` reads NO ledger `doc_type`s — physique = anchor + prod − shipped − eshop − taproom. So BC credits did NOT auto-replenish physique (they only affect the burn-velocity engine, which nets all doc_types). Therefore the restock leg is genuinely **ADDITIVE** (a new returns-in flow), NOT a suppression/avoid-double-count. The Q1 correction was right.
- **Beer-vs-deposit split = `ref_skus.recipe_id IS NOT NULL`** (CAUF/CAUAL/CO2 have NO recipe → deposit lines). Beer-credit lines = the returned FG; deposit lines ≈ all kegs back. The queue lists only beer-SKU lines.

**P0 — SCHEMA (APPLIED LIVE):**
- mig **373** `373_ord_returns.sql` — `ord_returns` (header) + `ord_return_lines` (`sku_id_fk` RESTRICT, `qty>0` CHECK, per-line disposition enum). Originally carried an order-XOR origin CHECK `chk_ord_returns_exactly_one_origin`. schema_meta rows added.
- mig **376** `376_returns_bc_derived_origin.sql` — the BC-derived pivot: **DROPPED the order-XOR CHECK**; **ADDED `origin_bc_document_no` + `origin_posting_date`** as the canonical origin (the avoir is the origin, not an order); **EXTENDED disposition enum to add `rebate`**; **ADDED `origin_ledger_sku_code`**. Both applied live. MIG HEAD now 376, next free = 377 (re-`migrate.php --status` at build start — parallel sessions live).

**P1 — DISPOSITION QUEUE (LIVE):** `?view=retours` in `public/modules/expeditions.php`. Lists beer-SKU `credit`/`return_receipt` ledger lines **awaiting disposition** (NOT EXISTS join on `bc_document_no` + `sku`), grouped by avoir; operator tags disposition per line (default **Quarantaine**). POST handler **re-queries the ledger for server-authoritative qty + posting_date** (operator CANNOT alter qty), **idempotent** (partial disposition supported — only un-dispositioned lines insert), txn + `log_revision`. CSS `exp-ret-*` in `expeditions.css`.

**P2 — FG RESTOCK LEG (LIVE + OPUS-VERIFIED):** `app/fg-stock.php`:
- **Step 6.7** (in `fg_stock_compute()`) + **Leg 4** (in `fg_stock_location_snapshot()`, 100% to the eshop-warehouse site, flagged `ASSUMPTION-restock-site-warehouse-2026-06-16`).

## 🆕 PART A/B/C BUILD SPEC — burn-rebate fix · returns RATE · OVERSELL/ATP tracker (PM architecture read 2026-06-16, Kouros-approved 3-part build; live-probed) — SPEC RETAINED; see AS-BUILT above for what shipped + the Part B sale_class deviation

**LEDGER FACTS (live-verified 2026-06-16, the SoT for all 3 parts):**
- `inv_sales_ledger.doc_type` ∈ {`shipment` (n=31543, qty_signed mostly NEG = depletion), `invoice` (n=6329, mostly NEG), `credit` (n=6619, mostly POS = reversal), `return_receipt` (n=18, mostly POS)}. **shipment & invoice are DISJOINT document populations (0 bc_document_no overlap at sku grain) — burn summing both does NOT double-count.**
- **SALES (depletion) doc_types = `shipment` + `invoice`** (negative qty_signed). **CREDIT/RETURN doc_types = `credit` + `return_receipt`** (positive). `qty_signed` IS the canonical unit basis (signed, SKU units).
- **BC gross-sold units (Part B denominator) = `GREATEST(0, -SUM(qty_signed)) WHERE doc_type IN ('shipment','invoice')`** for the same SKU population. (The burn engine's blanket all-doc_type sum is NET, not gross — for a RATE denominator you want GROSS sales, NOT net-of-returns.)
- **Returns numerator population (canonical, from returns-synthese.php pending_count, lines 100-114):** `doc_type IN ('credit','return_receipt') AND qty_signed>0 AND sku_id_fk IS NOT NULL AND ref_skus.recipe_id IS NOT NULL` (beer-only — same `recipe_id NOT NULL` beer filter the arc already uses). Matches the dispositioned-units population exactly.

**LEDGER↔RETURN_LINE LINKAGE (canonical, no cleaner key exists):** `ord_returns.origin_bc_document_no = inv_sales_ledger.bc_document_no` AND `ord_return_lines.sku_id_fk = inv_sales_ledger.sku_id_fk`. There is NO direct ledger-row FK on ord_return_lines (it carries `origin_ledger_sku_code` VARCHAR for display only, NOT an id FK). `ord_returns` DOES carry `origin_order_id_fk`/`origin_sales_order_id_fk` but those point at ord_orders/inv_sales_orders, NOT the ledger. **So bc_document_no + sku_id_fk IS the right and only join key** — it is exactly what returns-synthese.php pending_count already uses (precedent set). Confirm dispatch agent reuses that idiom, doesn't invent a new join.

**CUSTOMER-TYPE CLASSIFICATION (the B3/C2 "don't guess" answer — DECISIVE):**
- `ref_customers.trade_channel` ENUM('on_trade','off_trade') — **THIS is the canonical event/on-premise vs retail field. on_trade = bars/restos/clubs/theatres/events (HoReCa); off_trade = retail/supermarkets (Manor/Coop/Aligro).** Verified by customer-name sampling.
- **BUT only ~23% populated overall (622 on_trade + 64 off_trade + 2375 NULL of 3061).** On the OPEN-ORDER book it's better: 53 on_trade + 6 off_trade + 17 NULL + 1 giveaway of 77.
- `ref_customers.sale_class` ENUM has an `'event'` value BUT it is **NOT meaningfully populated — 3055 of 3061 customers are 'b2b'**, 1 each of the rest. **sale_class does NOT distinguish event vs retail. DO NOT use it for the customer-type cut.** (It IS valid for the existing `customs_artifact` exclusion only.)
- **RULING: the customer-type cut = `ref_customers.trade_channel` (on_trade vs off_trade), with a 3rd explicit `NULL/inconnu` bucket — NEVER fold NULL into either side, NEVER derive channel from sale_class or guess from name.** eshop is mixed INTO on_trade (e.g. "La Nébuleuse - ESHOP (privé)") so trade_channel ≠ a clean eshop discriminator; eshop/taproom are their own depletion legs (inv_sales_orders / inv_sales_bc), not B2B orders. **KOUROS-DECISION NEEDED: is the on_trade≈event proxy good enough, or should we (i) backfill trade_channel as part of the recurring BC→ref_customers sync, or (ii) add a finer segment column? SURFACE — do not let Sonnet guess.** Until then, present the cut as "on-premise (on-trade) / retail (off-trade) / non classé" with the NULL count visible so the operator sees coverage.

**PART A — burn over-net rebate fix (`app/seasonal-burn.php`):**
- **3 netting sites, not 2:** `sb_family_weekly_series` (~L108-120), `sb_all_sku_levels` window query (~L434-450), AND its **lifetime-stats query (~L455-465)** also nets all doc_types (first_sale/last_sale/lived_full_summer). The lifetime query doesn't sum qty so a rebate row only affects first/last-sale dates marginally — but apply the SAME exclusion to all 3 for consistency.
- **FIX SHAPE (confirmed):** add to each `WHERE` a `NOT EXISTS` correlated subquery excluding ledger rows that are credit/return AND dispositioned 'rebate': `AND NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM ord_returns r JOIN ord_return_lines rl ON rl.return_id_fk=r.id WHERE r.origin_bc_document_no = l.bc_document_no AND rl.sku_id_fk = l.sku_id_fk AND rl.disposition='rebate')`. (bc_document_no+sku join — same key as everywhere.) Only credit/return rows can match a return_line so no need to also gate doc_type inside the subquery, but adding `AND l.doc_type IN ('credit','return_receipt')` to the NOT-EXISTS guard makes intent explicit and keeps the planner honest.
- **RISK TO `6228e8a` / cron: ZERO.** The seasonal-index cron (`/etc/cron.d/maltytask-seasonal-index`, currently DISABLED) only writes `kpi_sku_seasonal_index` (the seasonal SHAPE per recipe×iso_week). It reads the same series; excluding rebate lines only sharpens the depletion signal. No schema change, no cron change. The forward sim consumes the level — a slightly higher (less-netted-down) burn = slightly more conservative runway = the intended correction.
- **MAGNITUDE / URGENCY (live): currently ZERO rebate lines dispositioned, and only 1 return line total (the Albaladejo restock=2). The leak is LATENT — it bites once the operator starts dispositioning the 3405-line beer-credit backlog as 'rebate'.** So Part A is correct to fix but is not yet distorting anything. Low urgency; ship with B/C.
- **EQUIP: sql + coder + webapp-testing** (read-only ?view=stock smoke; verify burn numbers unchanged today since 0 rebates, and that a synthetic rebate row drops out of the series).

**PART B — returns RATE (board-spec: returned ÷ BC gross-sold, same SKU pop, trailing-12mo, per-beer + per-customer-type, disposition MIX still leads, CHF in finance view only):**
- **DECISION: EXTEND `returns_synthese()` with a `rate` block, do NOT create a separate fn.** Single-source the returns aggregates (the file's stated purpose, lines 4-6). But the rate block runs on a DIFFERENT window (12mo) than the mix (90d) — so the fn signature grows a 2nd param OR computes both windows internally. **Cleanest: keep `$periodDays` for mix/by_client/by_beer (90d default) AND add the rate block on a hardcoded trailing-365d window internally** (mirrors how pending_count already pins its own 180d window regardless of $periodDays — same precedent, lines 97-99). So: mix=90d, rate=12mo, both in one fn, each documenting its window. **Do NOT unify the windows** — they answer different questions (operational recency vs annualized rate) and the board asked for 12mo rate explicitly.
- **Numerator (12mo):** dispositioned returned units `restock+scrap+quarantine` (rebate EXCLUDED — it's non-physical) over trailing 365d, per beer (`ref_recipes.name` via `ref_skus.recipe_id`) and per customer-type (`trade_channel`). **CAVEAT: only 1 line dispositioned today → the rate is ~0 until the backlog is triaged. The rate is only meaningful once dispositioning catches up.** Surface that honestly (e.g. "basé sur N retours traités" + the pending backlog count) so the operator doesn't read a fake-low rate.
- **Denominator (12mo, MUST match numerator population):** `GREATEST(0,-SUM(qty_signed)) WHERE doc_type IN ('shipment','invoice') AND sku_id_fk IS NOT NULL AND ref_skus.recipe_id IS NOT NULL`, same trailing-365d, grouped per beer and per trade_channel. GROSS sales (not net). Exclude `sale_class='customs_artifact'` to match the burn-engine channel hygiene.
- **per-customer-type:** group both num and denom by `ref_customers.trade_channel` resolved via `inv_sales_ledger.customer_id_fk` (returns side: via the bc_document_no→ledger→customer hop already in by_client). 3 buckets: on_trade / off_trade / NULL(non classé). Show coverage.
- **CHF / contra-revenue: NOT in returns_synthese() — finance view only.** Do not blend CHF into the volume/rate panel. (BC owns revenue; the avoir already reverses it. Any CHF view reads BC, not this fn.)
- **KOUROS-DECISION: the 90d-mix vs 12mo-rate dual window on KPI #283 / the Retours panel** — confirm he wants BOTH shown (mix headline 90d + rate 12mo sub-block) vs unifying. PM rec = keep both (matches his memo: "disposition MIX still leading" + "rate trailing-12mo").
- **EQUIP: sql + coder + ui + webapp-testing.**

**PART C — OVERSELL / ATP-breach tracking (the big one):**
- **Q1 — `flag_survendu` ALREADY == an ATP breach.** Exact def `app/fg-stock.php` L955: `'flag_survendu' => $liveFutur < 0` where `live_futur = physique − open_total_qty` (L905/947). `physique` = anchor + prod(historical, since-anchor) − expedie − eshop − taproom + repack + restock (on-hand FG). `open_total_qty` = `SUM(ord_order_lines.qty) JOIN ord_orders WHERE status NOT IN('shipped','cancelled') AND line_status='to_fulfil'` (Step 7, L702-712). **So flag_survendu = "committed open orders exceed on-hand FG" = ATP breach WITHOUT a scheduled-production term.** The board's ATP = on-hand + scheduled-production − committed; the current flag is the STRICTER on-hand−committed (no future-prod credit). There is NO scheduled/future-production input in fg_stock_compute today (prod is historical-since-anchor only, already in physique). **So we do NOT build a parallel oversell calc — flag_survendu IS it.** Magnitude = `-live_futur` (units short) when negative; attribution comes from the open_book per-SKU (Step 7 `$openBookBySku`, has per-order date/qty/status — extend to carry customer trade_channel).
- **Q2 — attribute oversell to EVENTS:** open orders ARE classifiable — `ord_orders.customer_id_fk → ref_customers.trade_channel`. Same answer as B3: `trade_channel` on_trade≈event/on-premise, off_trade=retail, NULL=non classé. On the open book it's 53/6/17/1 of 77 — usable but with a NULL bucket. **Same KOUROS-DECISION as B3 (is on_trade≈event good enough / backfill / finer column). Do NOT guess.** `ord_orders.internal_channel` (taproom/eshop/cage/shop) is only for `order_type='internal'` — all 77 open orders are `order_type='customer'` so internal_channel is NULL throughout; not the discriminator.
- **Q3 — WHERE oversell lives (cleanest, reusable):** **(a) a new KPI tracker reading the EXISTING `fg_stock_compute()` output (like #283) — YES, primary.** The engine already emits per-SKU `flag_survendu`, `live_futur`, `open_total_qty`, `couverture.open_book`. A new handler `kpi_logi_oversell` (or similar) calls `fg_stock_compute()`, counts `flag_survendu` SKUs, sums `-live_futur` (units short), and buckets the open_book by trade_channel. NO new compute path. **(b) a panel on the existing Couverture drilldown — secondary, cheap (the data is already in the couverture payload).** **Build (a) the KPI tracker as the headline; optionally surface the per-SKU short list on the Couverture face.** Do NOT add a 2nd derivation — read fg_stock_compute, period.
- **Q4 — HISTORICAL capture: NONE EXISTS. The engine is a pure current/forward snapshot.** `kpi_sku_seasonal_index` stores only the seasonal multiplier (recipe×iso_week×index), NOT any survendu/ATP outcome over time. There is NO table recording past oversell incidents. **To track "how often we oversold in high season" you MUST start snapshotting — that is a NEW, SEPARATE concern (a daily/weekly `ops_oversell_snapshot`-type table: date, sku_id_fk, live_futur, units_short, on_trade_short, off_trade_short).** A flock'd daily PHP cron calling fg_stock_compute() and persisting the negative-ATP rows (clone the credential-expiry / seasonal-index cron pattern, deployed DISABLED). **THIS IS A KOUROS SCOPE DECISION: the live tracker (Q3a) ships now off existing output; the time-series (snapshotting for "frequency in high season") is a distinct follow-on build — confirm he wants it in this arc or as a separate one.** PM rec: ship the live tracker now; propose the snapshot table as a fast-follow once he confirms he wants the historical frequency metric.
- **DIVERGENCE GUARD: there is exactly ONE FG/ATP derivation (`fg_stock_compute`). Any oversell tracker/panel/snapshot MUST read it — never recompute open-orders-vs-stock independently (that's the parallel-store anti-pattern).** The Step-7 open-order filter (`status NOT IN('shipped','cancelled') AND line_status='to_fulfil'`) is the canonical "committed" definition — reuse it, don't redefine.
- **EQUIP: sql + coder + ui + webapp-testing** (+ a separate sql+coder dispatch for the snapshot table/cron IF Kouros greenlights Q4).

## 📋 DEFERRED BACKLOG — operator-confirmed-WANTED, not abandoned (confirmed 2026-06-16; pick up later)

Both surface in the **visible unresolved tail** (refuse-don't-NULL holds — nothing silently mis-decomposes), so this is a COMPLETENESS gap, not a correctness hazard. **LOW volume.** Architecture verdict: extends the existing variant-bridge + the bundle→(recipe,container) decomposition already shipped in this arc — no new table, no parallel store; a qty-mult column on the bridge resolution + a promo/zero-price line classifier. Belongs squarely in the Shopify-fulfilment decomposition lane. Gate: none hard — pick up when the unresolved tail accumulates enough of these to matter. A small admin UI (list unmapped variants → pick a `ref_skus` row → write the bridge row) closes the loop without an SQL round-trip. **Convenience, not blocking** — the manual seed path works and the tail keeps it honest. Architecture verdict: pure CRUD over `ref_sku_shopify_variants` with a `ref_skus` whitelist (refuse-don't-NULL — no free-text SKU); add a `ref_pages` row + preset grant + RULE-3 tour card on ship. Gate: none; ship when variant volume makes manual seeding annoying. EQUIP sql+coder+ui+webapp-testing.

## ✅ §RETURNS REVERSAL POLLUTION FIX — SHIPPED 2026-06-16 (`5c911b7`, pushed origin/main)

**AS-BUILT (landed 2026-06-16, commit `5c911b7`, pushed; canaries Opus-verified on VPS, not agent-reported):**
- **Mig 387 `387_v_physical_returns.sql`** (applied; mig HEAD now 388 — 388 = parallel `388_smoketest_manager_bot` session, ignore). VIEW body = `SELECT l.* FROM inv_sales_ledger l WHERE doc_type IN ('credit','return_receipt') AND qty_signed>0 AND sku_id_fk IS NOT NULL`, with TWO `NOT EXISTS` exclusions — (a) same-day booking reversals: a shipment/invoice line for same `customer_id_fk` + `sku_id_fk` on the same `posting_date`; (b) rebate-tagged lines via `ord_return_lines.disposition='rebate'`. Supporting composite index **`ix_isl_revcheck (customer_id_fk, sku_id_fk, posting_date, doc_type)`**. schema_meta row added. **VERIFIED LIVE: view = 1 505 physical-return lines; schema_meta=1; index present.**
- **`app/returns-synthese.php`**: `'rate'` numerator AND `'overship'` watchlist numerator repointed to `v_physical_returns`. **`mix` / `by_client` / `by_beer` / `pending_count` LEFT UNCHANGED** — `pending_count` intentionally NOT view-backed yet, kept consistent with the disposition queue (still deferred behind the parallel "set-site" expeditions.php session). NB: this means the view did NOT yet subsume the rebate copy-paste at by_client/by_beer/mix (RULE-1 scrap deferred with the disposition-queue batch below).
- **CANARIES (Opus-verified VPS):** return rate corrected **6.60% → 1.818%** (returned_units 14 712 → 4 050); **FWT Management SA dropped off the over-ship watchlist** (was rank ~6 @ 82.3%); overship watchlist now **25 customers over the 12-unit floor**, top over-shippers are festivals/events — Assoc Trace-Ecart 92.9%, Saubrazil 77.8%, Paléo 69.3%, Blues en scène (1112 shipped/542 ret) 48.7%, Forget Yesterday (1139/520) 45.7% — predominantly `trade_channel='non classé'`, confirming refinement #1 (bulk-tag ~40 event customers `on_trade`) is the next data-cleanup.

**🔑 DURABLE KEY FINDING (re-stated as confirmed):** same-day customer+SKU booking reversals are an **ONGOING BC workflow** (BC posts shipment → credits it → re-invoices), **~72% of raw beer "returns"**, sourced from the recurring "Écritures comptables article.xlsx" export. `doc_type_raw` cannot distinguish them. **RE-1 follow-on:** add `is_reversal`/`reversed_doc_no` flag at BC-API ingest (deterministic pairing), then flip the view body `NOT EXISTS`-on-same-day → `is_reversal=0`, ZERO consumer change. (This follow-on also lives in the RE-1 BC-API arc.)

**🟡 STILL DEFERRED (behind parallel set-site `expeditions.php` session — repoint as ONE batch so count↔queue stay consistent):** (a) disposition queue render (~L2599); (b) processed list (~L2649); (c) POST handler reversal-guard (~L1532, the critical hazard — an operator restocking a reversal line would feed Leg 4 phantom FG); (d) synthèse `pending_count` → `v_physical_returns`. Plus UI wiring (oversell KPI tracker, returns-rate panel, oversell short-list on Couverture). When this batch lands, also collapse the by_client/by_beer/mix rebate copy-paste into the view (RULE-1 scrap, currently deferred).

## 🔴 §RETURNS REVERSAL POLLUTION FIX — ORIGINAL PM SPEC 2026-06-16 (retained for the rationale; build LANDED above)

**FINDING (verified live, 365d, beer SKUs `rs.recipe_id IS NOT NULL`).** The returns RATE block (`returns-synthese.php` `e76e21a`), the over-ship watchlist, the synthèse `pending_count`, AND the P1 disposition queue in `expeditions.php` count GROSS `credit`/`return_receipt` ledger lines as physical returns. **72.5% are SAME-DAY BOOKING REVERSALS** — a credit posted same day as a shipment/invoice to the same customer for the same SKU (BC posts shipment(−N) → credits it(+N) → re-invoices).
- GROSS returns 365d = **14 712 units / 800 lines**; SAME-DAY reversals = **10 662 units / 468 lines** (72.5%).
- FWT Management: 926 gross "returns" = **926 same-day reversals**, ~9 real.
- CORRECTED overall rate = **1.82%** (real 4 050 / sold 222 792) vs polluted 6.6%.
- **Reversals are an ONGOING BC workflow** — same-day-reversal lines spread continuously across EVERY posting month 2025-06→2026-06 (10–80/mo). The `imported_at` clustering on 2026-06-10 is just the bulk historical-load date; posting_date distribution is what matters and it's continuous. ⇒ a read-time filter is durable AND every future BC pull stays clean *as long as consumers go through the canonical accessor*.

**🔴 `bc_source_no` does NOT work as the reversal key** (corrects the finding's premise). On these rows `bc_source_no` holds a CUSTOMER/source number (3660, 2161, 1293…), NOT the reversed sales-doc number; 0 credits join to a shipment `bc_document_no` via it. The reliable signal is the same-day cust+sku+opposing-sign match. Do NOT build the filter on `bc_source_no` — it would match nothing and exclude zero reversals.

**PM RULINGS (the 5 questions):**
1. **Canonical home = SQL VIEW `v_physical_returns`**, NOT a PHP-helper-returning-a-predicate-string. The predicate is needed in raw SQL across 6+ sites with different aliases (`l.`/`cr.`/`l2.`); a view is the callable canonical accessor for SQL consumers ([call-the-accessor-not-copy] rule). `maltytask_app` HAS `CREATE VIEW`/`SHOW VIEW` (granted 2026-05-26). The view bakes in BOTH the reversal-exclusion AND the existing rebate `disposition='rebate'` NOT-EXISTS, subsuming the current copy-paste of the rebate predicate across ~5 synthese sites + 2 expeditions sites = RULE-1 scrap win. +`schema_meta` row (derived_view, read-only). Optionally a sibling `v_sold_beer_units` for the denominator (symmetry; low cost). Reversal predicate (verified 4050 kept / 10662 excluded):
   ```sql
   AND NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM inv_sales_ledger sh
     WHERE sh.doc_type IN ('shipment','invoice')
       AND sh.posting_date=l.posting_date AND sh.customer_id_fk=l.customer_id_fk
       AND sh.sku_id_fk=l.sku_id_fk AND sh.qty_signed<0)
   ```
2. **Read-time VIEW now (durable) + ingest-flag in RE-1 (follow-on).** Now: the view IS the durable fix — fast (composite idx `(posting_date,customer_id_fk,sku_id_fk,doc_type)`, EXPLAIN-verify), safe, zero-backfill, self-sustaining. RE-1 (BC API auto-pull): add `inv_sales_ledger.is_reversal TINYINT` + `reversed_doc_no VARCHAR`, stamp at load (ingest has both rows of a doc in hand → deterministic pairing, better than the same-day heuristic). At that point the view body flips `NOT EXISTS`→`WHERE is_reversal=0` and NO consumer changes — that's the payoff of the view. Record as RE-1 follow-on; don't block today's fix.
3. **BURN/`flag_survendu` SAFE — leave alone, do NOT route through the view.** `seasonal-burn.php` L108–126 `GREATEST(0,-SUM(qty_signed))` nets a same-day −N/+N pair to 0 (self-correcting). Burn wants NET physical depletion (legitimately includes real returns adding stock back); the view is a GROSS physical-return lens — different question, must not be unified (same rationale as the code's existing divergence-from-`v_sales_ledger_order_lines` comment). `fg_stock_compute` reads NO return doc_types → safe alone. **BUT the P1 disposition POST resolver (`expeditions.php` ~L1532) is the REAL hazard**: a reversal sits in the queue today; if an operator dispositions it `restock`, Leg 4 adds phantom kegs to physique that were never returned → real FG corruption. ⇒ the canonical filter MUST reach L1532 (the POST that feeds Leg 4), not only the L2599 render. This upgrades the queue fix from cosmetic to load-bearing.
4. **DUP sale-doc — NOT applicable to the beer rate; drop from this build.** The "436 groups / 8 060 units" is almost entirely NULL-`sku_id_fk` / non-beer rows, already excluded by `rs.recipe_id IS NOT NULL`. Beer-only excess = **20 groups / ~43 units**, and those are NOT clones (distinct `bc_line_seq` + distinct `sales_amount_chf`, e.g. a chf=0 pick line + a chf=97.80 priced line under one EXPED doc) = legitimate BC multi-line structure. A read `DISTINCT` would FALSE-REJECT real lines (the `inv_deliveries` coarse-UNIQUE lesson). Do NOT dedup. 43u on a 222 792 base = rounding error.
5. **No pre-existing returns view to extend.** `returns_synthese()` is the only aggregation home; the rebate NOT-EXISTS is copy-pasted across ~5 synthese sites + 2 expeditions queue sites — the view subsumes that duplication.

**BUILD SPEC.** Migration (next free; re-`migrate.php --status`): (1) `CREATE VIEW v_physical_returns` (beer credit/return_receipt, qty_signed>0, recipe_id NOT NULL, sku_id_fk NOT NULL, minus same-day-reversal NOT-EXISTS, minus rebate-disposition NOT-EXISTS; expose id/posting_date/bc_document_no/customer_id_fk/sku_id_fk/qty_signed/recipe_id); (2) composite idx above (INPLACE; no IF NOT EXISTS on the ALTER); (3) schema_meta row(s). Code: `returns-synthese.php` repoint rate numerator + per-beer-num + per-channel-num + overship returned_units + the `pending_count` ledger-side query (L103) at the view (remove now-redundant inline rebate NOT-EXISTS; denominators stay base-table shipment/invoice). `expeditions.php` route ALL three ledger-return sites through the view — P1 queue render (~L2599), **P1 disposition POST resolver (~L1532, critical)**, processed list (~L2649). `seasonal-burn.php`/`fg_stock_compute` NO CHANGE (+1-line comment noting reversals intentionally retained in net-depletion, excluded only from the gross-return lens).

**VERIFY (Opus independently — COGS/FG-adjacent, don't trust agent gate-PASS):** view unit-sum == 4 050 real / overall rate 1.82% (4050/222792); 10 662 fewer than gross; FWT through view ~9 (not 926); P1 queue count ~413→~110–130; burn `sb_forward_sim` byte-identical before/after on a sample recipe; POST resolver REFUSES a synthetic reversal line (un-restockable); idempotent re-run; `php -l` clean; md5 local↔VPS each deployed file; `?view=retours` 200 + synthèse panel renders corrected rate.

**KOUROS-DECISIONS:** (a) view the denominator too (rec: yes, symmetry) or inline; (b) approve RE-1 ingest-flag intent now, build at BC-API time (rec); (c) confirm the ~413→~130 queue shrink is expected (reversals were never physical returns → correct to vanish).

**EQUIP: sql + coder + ui + webapp-testing.**

## ✅ §COBRA DISTRIBUTOR IDENTITY — `ref_customer_identity` BILLING-ALIAS LINK — SHIPPED 2026-06-16 (mig 389; applied to prod; NOT git-committed/pushed — left for Kouros review)

**DURABLE ARCHITECTURAL FACT (Cobra distribution model).** La Nébuleuse's big-retail customers are BILLED via distributor **Cobra Traders**. BC books each order under a `Cobra Traders - X` sub-account (the **bill-to**); WeeklyOrders import + operators separately entered the SAME shipment under the geographic store account (the **ship-to**). Two distinct `ref_customers` rows for one economic order → the BC connector's collision-skip (keyed on `customer_id_fk`) never fired → **DUPLICATE orders**. Proven by ledger bill-to test: 100% of `inv_sales_ledger` sales post under Cobra-X accounts; the geographic store accounts carry ZERO direct billing (= pure ship-to shells).

**FIX (PM spec, executed):**
1. **mig 389 `ref_customer_identity`** — NON-destructive link table (NOT a merge): `member_customer_id_fk` UNIQUE → `canonical_customer_id_fk`, `relation` ENUM `'billing_alias'`, both FKs INT UNSIGNED → `ref_customers.id`; `schema_meta` row `table_class='reference'` `corrections_policy='allowed'`. **Both accounts stay `is_active=1`; `sync_bc_customers.py` UNTOUCHED.** A merge tool was REJECTED — it would tombstone one side → perpetual drift-review noise.
   - Seeded **40 links**: 756 ALIGRO ← 316/2414/2415/2416; 755 COOP ← 343/369/578/579 + 2417-2438 (26); 993 MIGROS ← 2439/2440; 760 MANOR ← 97/262/263/277/289/331/646; 934 WITTICH ← 94.
2. **EXCLUSIONS (operator rule + ledger evidence — NOT linked):** Migros Partenaire ×10 (DIRECT delivery, not via Cobra — Kouros's explicit carve-out), Migros Golf 1667 (golf-parc name collision), Cooper SA 323 + Coopérative Le Bled 2305 (other entities), Volg 944/949 (billed direct + no Cobra-VOLG account); Lidl/Aldi/Denner/Otto's have no geographic member accounts.
3. **Connector `scripts/python/ingest_bc_sales_orders.py`** — added `load_customer_identity_map()` + `canon(cid)` collapses BOTH sides of `detect_collisions()` to canonical. Dry-run: ORD210067/68 now SKIP-COLLISION (matched to kept #52/#53). Resurrection verified NOT a risk: `_REFRESH_LINE_STATUSES={entered,confirmed}` → `upsert_order` returns 'skip' for cancelled; UPDATE branch + `write_bc_mirror_fields()` never write status (Ruling-4 intact).
4. **Cleanup:** cancelled the duplicate BC echoes #142/#143 (status='cancelled' + `ord_order_status_events` + `log_revision`, FG-neutral; one-shot script removed local+VPS post-run).

**VERIFIED FINAL:** #52 shipped + #53 bl_printed ACTIVE; #142/#143 cancelled; `ref_customer_identity`=40 rows; mig 389 recorded; FK 40/40 OK.

**🔴 REUSABLE RULE (future brand extension):** confirm Cobra-distribution via the **ledger bill-to test** (do all the brand's sales post under a Cobra-X account, with the geographic account carrying zero direct billing?) **+ operator confirmation** — NEVER guess membership by name prefix. (Same never-guess-a-mapping discipline; geographic name match is a HINT, not proof — Migros Golf / Cooper SA / Le Bled are the name-collision counterexamples.)
